2:30:1649:28:28:273:338:616:12:Times:12:Times:ABSTRACT
2:31:1657:28:14:72:540:588:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:This paper develops a model to analyze information aggregation in commodity markets. Through centralized
2:32:1761:14:14:72:540:574:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:trading, commodity prices aggregate dispersed information about the strength of the global economy
2:33:1859:14:14:72:540:560:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:among goods producers whose production has complementarity, and serve as price signals to guide
2:34:1954:14:14:72:540:546:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:producers' production decisions and commodity demand. Our analysis highlights important feedback
2:35:2050:14:14:72:540:532:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:effects of informational noise originating from supply shocks and futures market trading on commodity
2:36:2151:14:42:72:532:518:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:demand and spot prices, which are ignored by existing empirical studies and policy discussions.
2:37:2246:42:14:72:148:476:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:Michael Sockin
2:38:2260:14:14:72:198:462:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:Department of Economics
2:39:2283:14:14:72:172:448:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:Princeton University
2:40:2303:14:14:72:170:434:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:Princeton, NJ 08540
2:41:2322:14:28:72:189:420:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:msockin@princeton.edu
2:42:2343:28:14:72:125:392:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:Wei Xiong
2:43:2352:14:14:72:172:378:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:Princeton University
2:44:2372:14:14:72:198:364:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:Department of Economics
2:45:2395:14:14:72:214:350:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:Bendheim Center for Finance
2:46:2422:14:14:72:173:336:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:Princeton, NJ  08450
2:47:2442:14:14:72:124:322:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:and NBER
2:48:2450:14:0:72:185:308:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:wxiong@princeton.edu
3:49:2470:0:20:89:540:708:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:The boom and bust cycles of commodity markets in 2007-2008 have stimulated intense
3:50:2552:20:20:72:540:688:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:academic and policy debate regarding the e§ects of supply and demand shocks and the role
3:51:2640:20:20:72:540:668:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:of futures market speculation.  Despite the attention given to these issues, the academic
3:52:2729:20:20:72:540:648:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:literature largely ignores a key aspect of commodity marketsó informational frictionsó by
3:53:2818:20:20:72:540:628:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:treating di§erent types of shocks as observable to market participants.  The markets for
3:54:2906:20:20:72:540:608:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:key industrial commodities, such as crude oil and copper, have become globalized in recent
3:55:2996:20:20:72:540:588:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:decades, with supply and demand now stemming from across the world. This globalization
3:56:3082:20:20:72:540:568:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:exposes market participants, who face signiÖcant informational frictions regarding the global
3:57:3175:20:20:72:540:548:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:supply, demand, and inventory of these commodities, to heightened uncertainty as to the
3:58:3262:20:20:72:540:528:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:strength of the global economy. In such an environment, commodity prices often serve as
3:59:3349:20:20:72:539:508:12:g_d0_f2:8:g_d0_f2:important price signals regarding the strength of the global economy for market participants.1
3:60:3443:20:20:89:540:488:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:This important informational role of commodity prices motivates several conceptual ques-
3:61:3531:20:19:72:540:468:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:tions not yet addressed by the existing economic literature: How do commodity markets
3:62:3616:19:20:72:540:449:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:aggregate information about the global economy?  How do informational frictions a§ect
3:63:3701:20:20:72:540:429:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:commodity prices and demand?  In response to signiÖcant commodity price volatility in
3:64:3786:20:20:72:540:409:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:recent years, policy circles have been concerned with speculation in commodity futures mar-
3:65:3877:20:20:72:540:389:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:kets. How does trading in futures markets a§ect spot prices and demand in the presence of
3:66:3966:20:20:72:191:369:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:informational frictions?
3:67:3990:20:20:89:540:349:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:This paper develops a theoretical framework to address these questions. Our framework
3:68:4075:20:20:72:540:329:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:integrates the standard models of asset market trading with asymmetric information, e.g.,
3:69:4164:20:20:72:540:309:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:Grossman and Stiglitz (1980) and Hellwig (1980), with an international macro setting, e.g.,
3:70:4255:20:20:72:540:289:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:Obstfeld and Rogo§ (1996) and Angeletos and LaíO (2013).  In this global economy, a
3:71:4338:20:20:72:540:269:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:continuum of specialized goods producers whose production has complementarity - which
3:72:4423:20:20:72:540:249:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:emerges from their need to trade produced goods with each other - demand a key commodity,
3:73:4512:20:20:72:540:229:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:such as copper, as a common production input. Through trading the commodity, the goods
3:74:4598:20:20:72:540:209:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:producers aggregate dispersed information regarding unobservable global economic strength,
3:75:4688:20:19:72:540:189:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:which ultimately determines their demand for the commodity. We start with a baseline model
3:76:4778:19:18:72:540:170:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:with only a spot market for the commodity to illustrate the key mechanism for informational
3:77:4869:18:16:85:539:152:7:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:1For example, in explaining the decision of the European Central Bank (ECB) to raise its key interest
3:78:4970:16:12:72:540:136:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:rate in March 2008 on the eve of the worst economic recession since the Great Depression, ECB policy
3:79:5070:12:12:72:540:124:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:reports cite high prices of oil and other commodities as a key factor, suggesting the signiÖcant ináuence of
3:80:5178:12:12:72:540:112:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:commodity prices on monetary policies. Furthermore, Hu and Xiong (2013) provide evidence that in recent
3:81:5281:12:12:72:540:100:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:years, stock prices across East Asian economies display signiÖcant and positive reactions to overnight futures
3:82:5391:12:12:72:540:88:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:price changes of a set of commodities traded in the U.S., suggesting that people across the world react to
3:83:5497:12:0:72:296:76:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:information contained in commodity futures prices.
4:84:5548:0:20:72:540:708:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:frictions to a§ect commodity markets, and then extend the model to incorporate a futures
4:85:5636:20:20:72:406:688:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:market to further characterize the role of futures market trading.
4:86:5702:20:20:89:540:668:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:Our baseline model focuses on a centralized spot market, through which the goods pro-
4:87:5787:20:20:72:540:648:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:ducers acquire the commodity from a group of suppliers, who are subject to an unobservable
4:88:5877:20:20:72:540:628:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:supply shock. The supply shock prevents the commodity price from perfectly aggregating
4:89:5963:20:20:72:540:608:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:the goods producersí information as to the global economic strength.  Nevertheless, the
4:90:6050:20:20:72:540:588:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:commodity price provides a useful signal to guide the producersíproduction decisions and
4:91:6138:20:20:72:540:568:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:commodity demand. Despite the non-linearity in the producersíproduction decisions, we
4:92:6223:20:20:72:540:548:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:derive a unique log-linear, noisy rational expectations equilibrium in closed form. In this
4:93:6314:20:20:72:540:528:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:equilibrium, each producerís commodity demand is a log-linear function of its private signal
4:94:6406:20:20:72:540:508:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:and the commodity price, while the commodity price is a log-linear function of the global
4:95:6495:20:20:72:540:488:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:economic strength and supply shock. This tractability originates from a key feature: the
4:96:6583:20:19:72:540:468:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:aggregate demand of a continuum of producers remains log-linear as a result of the law of
4:97:6672:19:20:72:147:449:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:large numbers.
4:98:6686:20:20:89:540:429:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:Through its informational role, a higher commodity price motivates each goods producer
4:99:6772:20:20:72:540:409:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:to produce more goods and thus demand more of the commodity as input, which o§sets
4:100:6854:20:20:72:540:389:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:the usual cost e§ect of a higher price leading to a lower quantity demanded. The comple-
4:101:6942:20:20:72:540:369:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:mentarity in production among goods producers magniÖes this informational e§ect through
4:102:7029:20:20:72:540:349:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:their incentives to coordinate production decisions.  Under certain conditions, our model
4:103:7118:20:20:72:540:329:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:shows that the informational e§ect can dominate the cost e§ect and lead to a positive price
4:104:7209:20:20:72:333:309:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:elasticity of producersídemand for the commodity.
4:105:7258:20:20:89:540:289:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:Again through its informational role, the commodity price allows the supply shock to
4:106:7342:20:20:72:540:269:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:have a subtle feedback e§ect on commodity demand and price.  In a perfect-information
4:107:7427:20:20:72:540:249:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:benchmark in which global economic strength and supply shocks are both observable, a
4:108:7511:20:20:72:540:229:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:higher supply shock leads to a lower commodity price and a larger quantity demanded
4:109:7594:20:20:72:540:209:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:by goods producers. However, in the presence of informational frictions, goods producers
4:110:7682:20:19:72:540:189:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:partially attribute the lower commodity price to a weaker global economy, which in turn
4:111:7769:19:20:72:540:170:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:induces them to reduce their commodity demand. This feedback e§ect thus further ampliÖes
4:112:7857:20:20:72:540:150:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:the negative price impact of the supply shock and undermines its impact on commodity
4:113:7941:20:20:72:116:130:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:demand.
4:114:7948:20:20:89:540:110:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:To estimate the e§ects of supply and demand shocks in commodity markets, it is common
4:115:8033:20:0:72:540:90:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:for the empirical literature to adopt structural models that ignore informational frictions by
5:116:8128:0:20:72:540:708:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:letting agents directly observe both demand and supply shocks.  As highlighted by our
5:117:8213:20:20:72:540:688:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:analysis, the price elasticity of demand and the e§ects of supply shocks are likely to be
5:118:8302:20:20:72:339:668:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:misspeciÖed when informational frictions are severe.
5:119:8354:20:20:89:540:648:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:In practice, trading commodity futures is appealing as it facilitates hedging and specula-
5:120:8444:20:20:72:540:628:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:tion without necessarily involving any physical delivery. However, whether and how traders
5:121:8534:20:20:72:540:608:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:in futures markets might a§ect commodity prices without taking or making any physical
5:122:8619:20:20:72:540:588:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:delivery remains illusive. To address this issue, our extended model incorporates a futures
5:123:8710:20:20:72:540:568:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:market, which allows one round of information aggregation among the goods producers be-
5:124:8797:20:20:72:540:548:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:fore commodity suppliers observe their supply shock and make physical delivery in the spot
5:125:8887:20:20:72:540:528:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:market. We also introduce to the futures market a group of Önancial traders, who always
5:126:8974:20:20:72:540:508:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:unwind their futures position before delivery and whose aggregate futures position is subject
5:127:9067:20:20:72:304:488:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:to random noise unrelated to the commodity.
5:128:9110:20:19:89:540:468:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:Interestingly, the futures price serves as a useful signal to the goods producers even
5:129:9196:19:20:72:540:449:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:though they also observe the spot price because the spot price and futures price are traded
5:130:9287:20:20:72:540:429:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:at di§erent times and are subject to di§erent noise: the spot price contains noise from
5:131:9374:20:20:72:540:409:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:commodity suppliersí supply shock, while the futures price contains noise from Önancial
5:132:9461:20:20:72:540:389:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:tradersífutures position. As a result, the futures price is not simply a shadow of the spot
5:133:9552:20:20:72:540:369:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:price. Instead, it has its own informational e§ects on commodity demand and the spot price.
5:134:9643:20:20:89:540:349:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:This result clariÖes a simple yet useful notion that futures market participants, even
5:135:9729:20:20:72:540:329:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:if not involved in physical delivery, can nevertheless impact commodity markets.  It also
5:136:9818:20:20:72:540:309:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:cautions against a commonly used empirical strategy based on commodity inventory to
5:137:9901:20:20:72:540:289:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:detect speculative e§ects, e.g., Kilian and Murphy (2010), Juvenal and Petrella (2012), and
5:138:9992:20:20:72:540:269:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:Knittel and Pindyck (2013). This strategy is premised on a widely held argument that if
5:139:10079:20:20:72:540:249:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:speculators distort the spot price of a commodity upward through futures market trading,
5:140:10167:20:20:72:540:229:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:consumers will Önd the commodity too expensive and thus reduce consumption, which in
5:141:10251:20:20:72:540:209:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:turn causes inventories of the commodity to spike. By assuming that consumers are able
5:142:10337:20:19:72:540:189:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:to recognize the commodity price distortion, this argument ignores realistic informational
5:143:10427:19:20:72:540:170:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:frictions faced by consumers, which are particularly relevant in times of great economic
5:144:10515:20:20:72:540:150:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:uncertainty. In contrast, our model shows that informational frictions may cause consumers
5:145:10605:20:20:72:514:130:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:to react to the distorted price by increasing rather than decreasing their consumption.
5:146:10692:20:20:89:540:110:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:Taken together, our analysis systematically illustrates how both spot and futures prices of
5:147:10783:20:0:72:540:90:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:key industrial commodities can serve as price signals for the strength of the global economy,
6:148:10877:0:20:72:540:708:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:which in turn allows supply shocks and noise from futures markets to feed back to commodity
6:149:10968:20:20:72:540:688:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:demand and spot prices. In doing so, our analysis provides a coherent argument for how the
6:150:11058:20:20:72:540:668:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:large ináow of investment capital to commodity futures markets might have ampliÖed the
6:151:11144:20:20:72:514:648:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:boom and bust of commodity prices in 2007-2008 by interfering with the price signals.
6:152:11229:20:20:89:540:628:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:Our model complements the recent macro literature that analyzes the role of informa-
6:153:11313:20:20:72:543:608:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:tional frictions on economic growth.  Lorenzoni (2009) shows that by ináuencing agentsí
6:154:11400:20:20:72:540:588:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:expectations, noise in public news can generate sizable aggregate volatility. Angeletos and
6:155:11491:20:20:72:540:568:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:LaíO (2013) focus on endogenous economic áuctuations that result from the lack of central-
6:156:11581:20:20:72:540:548:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:ized communication channels to coordinate the expectations of di§erent households. Our
6:157:11667:20:20:72:540:528:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:model adopts the setting of Angeletos and LaíO (2013) for the goods market equilibrium to
6:158:11756:20:20:72:540:508:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:derive endogenous complementarity in goods producersíproduction decisions. We analyze
6:159:11841:20:20:72:540:488:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:information aggregation through centralized commodity trading, which is absent from their
6:160:11930:20:19:72:421:468:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:model, and the feedback e§ects of the equilibrium commodity price.
6:161:11996:19:20:89:540:449:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:The literature has long recognized that trading in Önancial markets aggregates informa-
6:162:12083:20:20:72:540:429:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:tion and the resulting prices can feed back to real world activities, e.g., Bray (1981) and
6:163:12174:20:20:72:540:409:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:Subrahmanyam and Titman (2001). More recently, the literature points out that such feed-
6:164:12262:20:20:72:543:389:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:back e§ects can be particularly strong in the presence of strategic complementarity in agentsí
6:165:12356:20:20:72:540:369:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:actions. Morris and Shin (2002) show that in such a setting, noise in public information has
6:166:12448:20:20:72:540:349:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:an ampliÖed e§ect on agentsíactions and thus on equilibrium outcomes. In our model, the
6:167:12535:20:20:72:540:329:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:spot and futures prices of the commodity serve such a role in feeding back noise to the goods
6:168:12628:20:20:72:540:309:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:producersíproduction decisions. Similar feedback e§ects are also modeled in several other
6:169:12717:20:20:72:540:289:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:contexts, such as from stock prices to Örm capital investment decisions and from exchange
6:170:12806:20:20:72:540:269:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:rates to policy choices of central banks (e.g., Ozdenoren, and Yuan (2008), Angeletos, Loren-
6:171:12899:20:20:72:540:249:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:zoni and Pavan (2010) and Goldstein, Ozdenoren, and Yuan (2011, 2012)). The log-linear
6:172:12985:20:20:72:540:229:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:equilibrium derived in our model makes the analysis of feedback e§ects particularly tractable.
6:173:13079:20:20:89:540:209:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:This paper also contributes to the emerging literature that analyzes whether the large
6:174:13165:20:19:72:540:189:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:ináow of Önancial investment to commodity futures markets in recent years may have a§ected
6:175:13255:19:20:72:540:170:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:commodity prices, e.g., Stoll and Whaley (2010), Tang and Xiong (2012), Singleton (2012),
6:176:13344:20:20:72:540:150:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:Cheng, Kirilenko, and Xiong (2012), Hamilton and Wu (2012), Kilian and Murphy (2012),
6:177:13429:20:20:72:540:130:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:and Henderson, Pearson, and Wang (2012). Building on realistic informational frictions, our
6:178:13520:20:20:72:540:110:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:model describes a speciÖc mechanism for trading in futures markets to a§ect commodity
6:179:13605:20:0:72:540:90:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:demand and spot prices. This mechanism echoes Singleton (2012), which emphasizes the
7:180:13690:0:48:204:407:512:12:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Figure 1:Structure of the Baseline Model
7:181:13730:48:20:72:540:464:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:importance of accounting for agentsíexpectations in order to explain the boom and bust
7:182:13816:20:20:72:281:444:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:cycles of commodity prices in 2007-2008.
7:183:13856:20:20:89:540:424:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:The paper is organized as follows. We Örst present the baseline model in Section 1, and
7:184:13943:20:20:72:540:404:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:then the extended model in Section 2. Section 3 concludes the paper. We provide all the
7:185:14030:20:39:72:243:384:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:technical proofs in the Appendix.
7:186:14063:39:32:72:271:345:17:g_d0_f3:17:g_d0_f3:1  The Baseline Model
7:187:14084:32:20:72:540:313:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:In this section we develop a baseline model with two dates= 12to analyze the e§ects of
7:188:14172:20:20:72:540:293:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:informational frictions on the market equilibrium related to a commodity. One can think of
7:189:14262:20:20:72:540:273:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:this commodity as crude oil or copper, which is used across the world as a key production
7:190:14351:20:20:72:540:253:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:input. We adopt a modiÖed setup of Angeletos and LaíO (2013) to model a continuum of
7:191:14435:20:20:72:539:233:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:islands of total mass1Each island produces a single good, which can either be consumed at
7:192:14525:20:20:72:540:213:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:ìhomeîor traded for another good produced ìawayîby another island. A key feature of the
7:193:14612:20:20:72:540:193:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:baseline model is that the commodity market is not only a place for market participants to
7:194:14702:20:19:72:540:173:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:trade the commodity but also a platform to aggregate private information about the strength
7:195:14793:19:35:72:535:154:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:of the global economy, which ultimately determines the global demand for the commodity.

14:448:26549:20:20:72:540:668:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f4:similar to Hellwig (1980). The commodity price also depends on the supply side noise-

14:450:26725:20:20:72:224:628:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:with asymmetric information.
14:451:26753:20:20:89:540:608:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:It is well-known that asset market equilibria with asymmetric information are often in-
14:452:26840:20:20:72:540:588:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:tractable due to the di¢ culty in aggregating di§erent participantsípositions. The existing
14:453:26931:20:20:72:540:568:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:literature commonly adopts the setting of Grossman and Stiglitz (1980) and Hellwig (1980),
14:454:27021:20:20:72:540:548:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:which features CARA utility for agents and normal distributions for asset fundamentals and
14:455:27111:20:20:72:540:528:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:noise trading. Under this setting, the equilibrium asset price is a linear function of the asset
14:456:27207:20:20:72:540:508:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:fundamental and the noise from noise trading, while each agentís asset position is a linear
14:457:27298:20:20:72:540:488:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:function of the price and his own signal. This setting is, however, unsuitable for analyzing
14:458:27390:20:19:72:540:468:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:real consequences of asset market trading as agentsíinvestment and production decisions
14:459:27477:19:20:72:420:449:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:tend to make asset fundamentals deviate from normal distributions.
14:460:27543:20:20:89:540:429:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:The log-linear equilibrium derived in Proposition 2 resembles the linear equilibrium of
14:461:27630:20:20:72:540:409:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:Grossman and Stiglitz (1980) and Hellwig (1980) but nevertheless incorporates real conse-
14:462:27719:20:20:72:540:389:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:quences of commodity market trading. In fact, each producerís commodity demand has a
14:463:27803:20:20:72:540:369:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:log-normal distribution (e.g., equation (11)). As shown by equation (33) in the Appendix,
14:464:27892:20:20:72:540:349:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:the producersíaggregate demand remains log-normal as a result of the law of large numbers.
14:465:27982:20:35:72:411:329:12:g_d0_f2:8:g_d0_f2:This is the key feature that ensures the tractability of our model.7
14:466:28050:35:22:72:337:294:14:g_d0_f3:14:g_d0_f3:1.3  E§ects of informational frictions
14:467:28088:22:28:72:297:272:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:1.3.1  Perfect-information benchmark

14:470:28304:20:20:72:540:205:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:modity supply shock-are both observable by all market participants.  Then, the goods

14:472:28479:20:18:72:335:165:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:following proposition characterizes this benchmark.

19:671:38019:20:33:72:333:688:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:fare relative to the perfect-information benchmark.

19:673:38157:20:31:71:385:635:12:g_d0_f20:12:g_d0_f20:strictly lower than that in the perfect-information benchmark.
19:674:38219:31:28:71:313:604:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:1.3.6  Implications for structural models
19:675:38260:28:20:71:539:576:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:The feedback e§ect of supply shock on commodity demand has important implications for
19:676:38345:20:20:71:539:556:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:studies of the e§ects of supply and demand shocks in commodity markets. For example,
19:677:38429:20:20:71:539:536:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:Hamilton (1983) emphasizes that disruptions to oil supply and the resulting oil price in-
19:678:38518:20:20:71:539:516:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:creases can have a signiÖcant impact on the real economy, while Kilian (2009) argues that
19:679:38607:20:20:71:539:496:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:aggregate demand shocks have a bigger impact on the oil market than previously thought. As
19:680:38697:20:20:71:539:476:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:supply and demand shocks have opposite e§ects on oil prices, it is important to isolate their
19:681:38790:20:19:71:539:456:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:respective e§ects. The existing literature commonly uses structural models to decompose
19:682:38877:19:20:71:539:437:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:di§erent types of shocks and then estimate their e§ects, e.g., Kilian (2009). The premise
19:683:38966:20:20:71:539:417:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:of these structural models is that, while researchers cannot directly observe the shocks that
19:684:39059:20:20:71:539:397:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:hit commodity markets, agents in the markets are able to perfectly observe the shocks and
19:685:39148:20:20:71:539:377:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:optimally respond to them. As a result, by imposing certain restrictions on how di§erent
19:686:39236:20:20:71:539:357:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:types of shocks a§ect the price of a commodity and its demand, researchers can infer realized
19:687:39329:20:20:71:446:337:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:shocks from observing the price and quantity of commodity transactions.
19:688:39400:20:20:89:540:317:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:As we discussed before, it is unrealistic to assume that agents in commodity markets can
19:689:39488:20:20:71:539:297:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:perfectly di§erentiate di§erent types of shocks. Our model shows that in the presence of
19:690:39576:20:20:71:539:277:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:informational frictions, supply shocks and demand shocks can have e§ects in sharp contrast
19:691:39666:20:20:71:539:257:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:to standard intuitions developed from perfect-information settings. For example, the price
19:692:39756:20:20:71:539:237:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:elasticity of commodity demand can be positive rather than negative, and supply shocks
19:693:39842:20:20:71:539:217:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:can reduce rather than increase demand for the commodity. These implications challenge
19:694:39928:20:20:71:539:197:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:identiÖcation restrictions commonly used in the existing structural models, such as the price
19:695:40021:20:19:71:539:177:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:elasticity of demand being negative and supply shocks having a positive impact on demand.
19:696:40110:19:20:71:539:158:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:Furthermore, our model shows that, by ignoring informational frictions, standard structural
19:697:40201:20:20:71:426:138:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:models are likely to underestimate the price impact of supply shocks.
19:698:40270:20:20:89:540:118:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:Taken together, our model motivates structural models to explicitly build in informational
19:699:40360:20:0:71:477:98:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:frictions in order to systematically isolate e§ects of supply and demand shocks.
20:700:40442:0:32:72:388:708:17:g_d0_f3:17:g_d0_f3:2  An Extended Model with Futures
20:701:40475:32:20:72:540:676:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:In practice, spot markets of commodities are typically decentralized, while centralized trad-
20:702:40568:20:20:72:540:656:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:ing often occurs in futures markets. As a result, futures markets play an important role in
20:703:40659:20:20:72:540:636:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:aggregating information regarding supply and demand of many commodities.10In this sec-
20:704:40745:20:20:72:540:616:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:tion, we extend our baseline model to incorporate a futures market. This extension allows
20:705:40834:20:20:72:540:596:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:us to examine how commodity futures prices can serve as price signals even when goods
20:706:40919:20:35:72:249:576:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:producers also observe spot prices.
20:707:40954:35:27:72:207:541:14:g_d0_f3:14:g_d0_f3:2.1  Model setting
20:708:40972:27:20:72:540:514:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:We again keep our extension to a minimal setting for analyzing the role of futures market
20:709:41061:20:20:72:540:494:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:trading in aggregating information. SpeciÖcally, we introduce a new date= 0before the
20:710:41147:20:20:71:539:474:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f5:two dates= 1and2in the baseline model, and a centralized futures market at= 0
20:711:41226:20:20:71:539:454:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:for delivery of the commodity at= 1All agents can take positions in the futures market
20:712:41314:20:20:71:539:434:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:at= 0, and can choose to revise or unwind their positions before delivery at= 1The
20:713:41399:20:20:71:539:414:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:áexibility to unwind positions before delivery is an advantage that makes futures market
20:714:41487:20:20:71:222:394:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:trading appealing in practice.
20:715:41517:20:20:89:540:374:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:We keep all of the agents in the baseline model: island households, goods producers,
20:716:41601:20:19:71:539:354:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:and commodity suppliers and add a group of Önancial traders. These traders invest in the
20:717:41689:19:20:71:540:335:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:commodity by taking a long position in the futures market at= 0and then unwinding this
20:718:41776:20:20:71:282:315:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:position at= 1without taking delivery.
20:719:41815:20:20:89:540:295:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:To focus on information aggregation through trading in the futures market, we assume
20:720:41899:20:20:71:539:275:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:that there is no spot market trading at= 0. At= 1a spot market naturally emerges
20:721:41982:20:20:71:539:255:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:through commodity delivery for the futures market.  Commodity suppliers take a short
20:722:42066:20:20:71:543:235:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:position in the futures market at= 0and then make delivery at= 1The suppliersí
20:723:42147:20:20:72:540:215:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:marginal cost of supplying the commodity determines the spot price. When a trader chooses
20:724:42236:20:48:72:502:195:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:to unwind a futures position at= 1his gain/loss is determined by this spot price.
20:725:42319:48:16:81:539:147:7:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:10Roll (1984) systematically analyzes the futures market of orange juice in e¢ ciently aggregating informa-
20:726:42426:16:12:72:540:131:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:tion about weather in Central Florida, which produces more than 98% of the U.S. orange output. Garbade
20:727:42528:12:12:72:540:119:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:and Silber (1983) provides evidence that futures markets play a more important role in information discovery
20:728:42636:12:0:72:263:107:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:than cash markets for a set of commodities.

22:820:46291:33:28:71:212:199:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:2.1.2  Financial traders
22:821:46315:28:20:71:539:171:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:Since the mid-2000s, commodity futures markets experienced a large expansion of Önancial
22:822:46403:20:20:71:539:151:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:traders as a result of a Önancialization process through which commodity futures became a
22:823:46492:20:20:71:539:131:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:new asset class for portfolio investors such as pension funds and endowments (e.g., Tang and
22:824:46584:20:20:71:539:111:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:Xiong, 2012). These investors regularly allocate a fraction of their portfolios to investing in
22:825:46679:20:19:71:539:91:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:commodity futures and swap contracts. They take only long positions and typically close out
22:826:46770:19:0:71:539:72:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:positions without taking any physical delivery. As a result, their trading does not directly
23:827:46864:0:20:72:540:708:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:a§ect the supply and demand of commodities. During the same period, hedge funds also
23:828:46948:20:20:72:540:688:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:expanded their trading operations in commodity futures markets. They are áexible in taking
23:829:47038:20:20:72:540:668:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:both long and short positions and usually do not hold physical commodities, even though
23:830:47125:20:20:72:231:648:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:they are allowed to in practice.
23:831:47157:20:20:89:540:628:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:To examine whether these Önancial traders can a§ect commodity prices, we introduce a

27:1046:57551:19:15:81:539:107:7:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:14Note that despite the futures price containing di§erent information content from the spot price, there

28:1061:57958:0:16:413:419:655:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:1

28:1064:57972:29:20:71:539:618:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:By using equation (61) in the proof of Proposition 8, the coe¢ cient of-in the aggregate
28:1065:58060:20:20:71:184:598:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:commodity demand is
28:1066:58079:20:25:250:360:578:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:+=0
28:1067:58093:25:20:72:416:553:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:Thus,-also has a positive e§ect on aggregate commodity demand.
28:1068:58155:20:20:89:540:533:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:The e§ects of-on commodity demand and the spot price clarify a simple yet important
28:1069:58238:20:20:72:540:513:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:conceptual point that traders in commodity futures markets, who never take or make physical
28:1070:58329:20:20:72:540:493:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:commodity delivery, can nevertheless impact commodity markets through the informational
28:1071:58416:20:30:72:309:473:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:feedback channel of commodity futures prices.
28:1072:58461:30:28:72:281:443:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:2.3.2  Detecting speculative e§ects
28:1073:58496:28:20:72:540:415:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:In the ongoing debate on whether speculation in commodity futures markets a§ected com-
28:1074:58582:20:20:72:540:395:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:modity prices during the commodity market boom and bust of 2007-2008, many studies, e.g.,
28:1075:58671:20:20:72:540:375:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:Kilian and Murphy (2010), Juvenal and Petrella (2012), and Knittel and Pindyck (2013),
28:1076:58757:20:20:72:540:355:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:adopt an inventory-based detection strategy. This strategy builds on a widely-held argument
28:1077:58848:20:20:72:540:335:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:that if speculators artiÖcially drive up the futures price of a commodity, say crude oil, then
28:1078:58942:20:20:72:540:315:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:the price spread between the futures price and the spot price of crude oil will motivate the
28:1079:59034:20:20:72:540:295:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:standard textbook cash-and-carry trades by some arbitrageurs. This in turn will cause the
28:1080:59123:20:19:72:540:275:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:spot price to rise with the futures price. Then, consumers will Önd consuming the commodity
28:1081:59214:19:20:72:456:256:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:too expensive and thus reduce consumption, causing oil inventory to spike.
28:1082:59288:20:20:89:540:236:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:Under this argument, price increases in the absence of any inventory increases are ex-
28:1083:59374:20:20:72:540:216:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:plained by fundamental demand. Thus, price e§ects induced by speculation should be limited
28:1084:59464:20:20:72:540:196:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:to price increases accompanied by contemporaneous inventory increases. Motivated by this
28:1085:59552:20:20:72:540:176:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:argument, the literature, as reviewed by Fattouh, Kilian and Mahadeva (2012), tends to use
28:1086:59642:20:20:72:540:156:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:the lack of any pronounced oil inventory spike before the peak of oil prices in July 2008 as
28:1087:59734:20:20:72:540:136:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:evidence to rule out any signiÖcant role played by futures market speculation during this
28:1088:59823:20:17:72:201:116:12:g_d0_f2:8:g_d0_f2:commodity price boom.15
28:1089:59846:17:16:81:539:99:7:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:15An exception in this structural VAR literature is Lombardi and Van Robays (2012), who allow non-
28:1090:59944:16:11:72:540:83:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:fundamental shocks to futures prices to cause the futures-spot spread to deviate from its no arbitrage
28:1091:60046:11:0:72:305:72:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:relationship because of frictions to inventory buildup.
29:1092:60103:0:20:89:540:708:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:Despite the intuitive appeal of this inventory-based detection strategy, it ignores impor-
29:1093:60193:20:20:72:540:688:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:tant informational frictions faced by consumers in reality. In particular, it implicitly assumes
29:1094:60289:20:20:72:540:668:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:that oil consumers observe the global economic fundamentals and are thus able to recognize
29:1095:60379:20:20:72:540:648:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:whether current oil prices are too high relative to the fundamentals in making their con-
29:1096:60468:20:20:72:540:628:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:sumption decisions. This assumption is strong and may prove unrealistic in certain periods
29:1097:60558:20:20:72:381:608:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:with great economic uncertainty and informational frictions.
29:1098:60618:20:20:89:540:588:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:Our model illustrates a contrasting example in the presence of informational frictions. In
29:1099:60708:20:20:72:540:568:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:this environment, commodity futures prices serve as important price signals. By ináuencing
29:1100:60798:20:20:72:540:548:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:consumersíbeliefs about global economic fundamentals, noise from futures market trading
29:1101:60885:20:20:72:540:528:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:can distort commodity demand and spot prices in the same direction, rather than opposite
29:1102:60973:20:20:72:540:508:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:directions. This insight thus weakens the power of the widely-used, inventory-based detection
29:1103:61066:20:20:72:467:488:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:strategy and cautions against over-interpreting any conclusion building on it.
29:1104:61144:20:19:89:540:468:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:Our model also conveys a broader message that in the presence of informational frictions,
29:1105:61233:19:20:72:540:449:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:commodity futures prices are not simply the shadow of the spot prices that reáect the spot
29:1106:61323:20:20:72:540:429:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:prices based on the standard no-arbitrage principle. Instead, commodity futures markets
29:1107:61410:20:20:72:540:409:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:may serve as central platforms for aggregating information, and the resulting futures prices
29:1108:61502:20:31:72:535:389:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:can feed back both valuable information and noise to commodity demand and spot prices.
29:1109:61588:31:27:72:442:358:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:2.3.3  Understanding the commodity price boom in 2007-2008
29:1110:61646:27:20:72:540:331:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:In the aftermath of the synchronized price boom and bust of major commodities in 2007-
29:1111:61732:20:20:72:540:311:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:2008, a popular view posits that the commodity price boom was the result of a bubble
29:1112:61816:20:20:72:540:291:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:caused by speculation in commodity futures markets (e.g., Masters (2008) and US Senate
29:1113:61902:20:20:72:540:271:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:Permanent Subcommittee on Investigations (2009)). According to this view, the large ináow
29:1114:61991:20:20:72:540:251:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:of investment capital to the long side of commodity futures markets before July 2008 led to
29:1115:62082:20:20:72:540:231:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:a huge price bubble detached from economic fundamentals that collapsed in the second half
29:1116:62171:20:20:72:540:211:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:of 2008. As we discussed earlier, the lack of evidence for reduced oil consumption during the
29:1117:62264:20:20:72:513:191:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:boom makes it di¢ cult for many economists to accept the oil price boom as a bubble.
29:1118:62348:20:20:89:540:171:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:Another view attributes the price boom to the combination of rapidly growing demand
29:1119:62431:20:20:72:540:151:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:from emerging economies and stagnant supply (e.g., Hamilton (2009)). This argument is
29:1120:62516:20:20:72:540:131:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:compelling for explaining the commodity price increases before 2008. However, oil prices
29:1121:62604:20:20:72:540:111:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:continued to rise over 40% from January to July 2008, to peak at $147 per barrel, at a time
29:1122:62695:20:19:72:540:91:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:when the U.S. had already entered a recession, Bear Stearns had collapsed in March, and
29:1123:62782:19:0:72:540:72:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:most other developed economies were already showing signs of weakness. While China and
30:1124:62870:0:20:72:540:708:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:other emerging economies remained strong at the time, it is di¢ cult to argue, in hindsight,
30:1125:62962:20:20:72:540:688:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:that their growth sped up enough to be able to o§set the clear weakness of the developed
30:1126:63050:20:20:72:334:668:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:economies and cause oil prices to rise another 40%.
30:1127:63101:20:20:89:540:648:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:The informational frictions faced by market participants can help us understand this
30:1128:63185:20:20:72:540:628:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:puzzling price episode. Due to the lack of reliable data on the strength of emerging economies,
30:1129:63280:20:20:72:540:608:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:it was di¢ cult at the time to precisely measure the strength of the emerging economies. As a
30:1130:63373:20:20:72:540:588:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:result, the prices of crude oil and other commodities were regarded as important price signals
30:1131:63467:20:20:72:540:568:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:(see evidence referenced in Footnote 1). This environment makes our model particularly
30:1132:63553:20:20:72:540:548:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:appealing in linking the large commodity price increases in early 2008 to the concurrent
30:1133:63641:20:20:72:540:528:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:large ináow of investment capital, motivated by the intention of many money managers
30:1134:63725:20:20:72:540:508:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:to diversify their portfolio out of declining stock markets into more promising commodity
30:1135:63814:20:20:72:540:488:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:futures markets, e.g., Tang and Xiong (2012). By pushing up commodity futures prices, and
30:1136:63903:20:19:72:540:468:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:sending a wrong price signal, the large investment áow might have confused goods producers
30:1137:63993:19:20:72:540:449:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:across the world into believing that emerging economies were stronger than they actually
30:1138:64081:20:20:72:540:429:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:were. This distorted expectation could have prevented the producers from reducing their
30:1139:64168:20:20:72:540:409:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:demand for the commodity despite the high commodity prices, which in turn made the high
30:1140:64255:20:20:72:540:389:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:prices sustainable. To the extent that more information corrected the producersíexpectations
30:1141:64347:20:20:72:540:369:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:over time, the high commodity prices persisted for several months and eventually collapsed
30:1142:64437:20:20:72:540:349:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:in the second half of 2008. Interestingly, after oil prices dropped from its peak of $147 to $40
30:1143:64533:20:20:72:540:329:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:per barrel at the end of 2008, oil demand largely evaporated and inventory piled up, despite
30:1144:64625:20:20:72:187:309:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:the much lower prices.
30:1145:64647:20:20:89:540:289:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:Taken together, the commodity price boom in 2007-2008 is not necessarily a price bubble
30:1146:64734:20:20:72:540:269:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:detached from economic fundamentals. Instead, it is plausible to argue that, in the presence
30:1147:64826:20:20:72:540:249:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:of severe informational frictions in early 2008, the large ináow of investment capital might
30:1148:64918:20:20:72:540:229:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:have distorted signals coming from commodity prices and led to confusion among market
30:1149:65003:20:20:72:540:209:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:participants about the strength of emerging economies. This confusion, in turn, could have
30:1150:65093:20:19:72:540:189:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:ampliÖed the boom and bust of commodity prices, which echoes the emphasis of Singleton
30:1151:65179:19:20:72:540:170:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:(2012) to account for agentsíexpectations in explaining the price cycle. To test this hy-
30:1152:65268:20:20:72:540:150:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:pothesis would require estimating a structural model that explicitly takes into account these
30:1153:65361:20:0:72:189:130:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:informational frictions.
31:1154:65387:0:28:72:327:708:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:2.3.4  Implication for market transparency
31:1155:65429:28:20:72:540:680:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:Information frictions in the futures market, originating from the unobservability of the po-
31:1156:65521:20:20:72:540:660:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:sitions of di§erent participants, are essential in order for the trading of Önancial traders to
31:1157:65616:20:20:72:540:640:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:impact the demand for the commodity and spot prices. The following proposition conÖrms
31:1158:65702:20:20:72:539:620:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:that as--! 1(i.e., the position of Önancial traders becomes publicly observable), the spot
31:1159:65792:20:33:72:423:600:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:market equilibrium converges to the perfect-information benchmark.
31:1160:65858:33:20:72:540:567:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f20:Proposition 9As--! 1the spot price and aggregate demand converge to the perfect-
31:1161:65939:20:32:72:194:547:12:g_d0_f20:12:g_d0_f20:information benchmark.
31:1162:65961:32:20:89:540:515:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:Proposition 9 shows that by improving transparency of the futures market, one can
31:1163:66042:20:20:72:540:495:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:achieve the perfect-information benchmark because by making the position of Önancial
31:1164:66126:20:20:72:540:475:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:traders publicly observable, the-noise no longer interferes with the information aggregation
31:1165:66218:20:20:71:539:455:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:in the futures market.  As a result, the futures price fully reveals the global fundamen-
31:1166:66307:20:20:71:539:435:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:tal, which, in turn, allows goods producers to achieve the same e¢ ciency allowed by the
31:1167:66395:20:20:71:539:415:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:perfect-information benchmark. This nice convergence result relies on the assumption that
31:1168:66484:20:20:71:540:395:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:the supply noise-does not a§ect the futures market trading at= 0and hits the spot mar-
31:1169:66571:20:20:72:540:375:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:ket only at= 1. Nevertheless, this result highlights the importance of improving market
31:1170:66659:20:20:72:148:355:12:g_d0_f2:8:g_d0_f2:transparency.16
31:1171:66674:20:20:89:540:335:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:Imposing position limits on speculators in commodity futures markets has occupied much
31:1172:66760:20:20:72:540:315:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:of the post-2008 policy debate, while improving market transparency has received much less
31:1173:66850:20:20:72:540:295:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:attention. By highlighting the feedback e§ect originating from information frictions as a
31:1174:66939:20:20:72:540:275:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:key channel for noise in futures market trading to a§ect commodity prices and demand,
31:1175:67024:20:19:72:540:255:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:our model suggests that imposing position limits may not address the central information
31:1176:67112:19:20:72:540:236:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:frictions that confront participants in commodity markets and thus may not be e§ective in
31:1177:67201:20:20:72:540:216:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:reducing any potential distortion caused by speculative trading. Instead, making trading
31:1178:67289:20:18:72:337:196:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:positions more transparent might be more e§ective.
31:1179:67339:18:16:81:539:178:7:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:16While our analysis focuses on the noise e§ect of their trading, Önancial traders can also contribute to
31:1180:67444:16:12:72:540:162:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:information aggregation. As-increases, the futures position of Önancial traders builds more on the global
31:1181:67549:12:12:71:539:150:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:economic fundamentallog.  Then, the futures pricelogbecomes more informative oflog.  This is
31:1182:67644:12:12:71:540:138:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:because one can prove based on Proposition 8 that~~-, the ratio of the loadings oflogonlogand-,
31:1183:67745:12:0:71:145:126:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:increases with-.
32:1184:67763:0:32:72:194:708:17:g_d0_f3:17:g_d0_f3:3  Conclusion
32:1185:67776:32:20:72:540:676:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:This paper develops a theoretical framework to analyze information aggregation in commod-
32:1186:67865:20:20:72:540:656:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:ity markets. Our baseline model features a commodity spot market to show that, through
32:1187:67951:20:20:72:540:636:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:the informational role of spot prices, the aggregate demand from goods producers can in-
32:1188:68039:20:20:72:540:616:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:crease with the spot price and the supply shock can have an ampliÖed e§ect on the price
32:1189:68126:20:20:72:540:596:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:and an undetermined e§ect on the quantity demanded. Our extended model further incor-
32:1190:68211:20:20:72:540:576:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:porates one round of futures market trading to show that futures prices can serve as an
32:1191:68298:20:20:72:540:556:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:important price signal, even though goods producers also observe spot prices. Through the
32:1192:68387:20:20:72:540:536:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:informational role of futures prices, noise in futures market trading can also interfere with
32:1193:68480:20:20:72:540:516:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:goods producersíexpectations and distort their production decisions. Taken together, our
32:1194:68568:20:19:72:540:496:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:analysis cautions empirical and policy studies of commodity markets to fully incorporate
32:1195:68656:19:20:72:540:477:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:realistic informational frictions faced by market participants across the world. Our analysis
32:1196:68749:20:20:72:540:457:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:also provides a coherent argument for how the large ináow of investment capital to commod-
32:1197:68839:20:20:72:540:437:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:ity futures markets, by jamming the commodity price signals and leading to confusion about
32:1198:68929:20:20:72:540:417:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:the strength of emerging economies, might have ampliÖed the boom and bust of commodity
32:1199:69015:20:76:72:173:397:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:prices in 2007-2008.
32:1200:69035:76:30:72:363:321:17:g_d0_f3:17:g_d0_f3:Appendix  Proofs of Propositions
